## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations)
**Analysis**: The task involves acceleration (dv_dt) as a function of position (x), velocity (v), and time (t), which is the governing second-order ODE for a mechanical oscillator. The physical context indicates nonlinear harmonic motion, so the equation of motion likely includes nonlinear restoring forces and/or nonlinear damping terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3
- Duffing oscillator with linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * x
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x
- Mixed Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v
- Forced harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x)
- General odd-polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v)
- Asymmetric restoring (even power): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2
- Nonlinear stiffness with quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * abs(v)
- Time-dependent external forcing with nonlinear stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force â†’ acceleration has a term proportional to x (often with negative coefficient)
- Linear damping â†’ term proportional to v (dissipative, typically negative sign)
- Symmetric nonlinear stiffness â†’ odd powers of x (x^3, x^5) indicating hard/soft spring behavior
- Asymmetric potential â†’ even powers of x (x^2) breaking leftâ€“right symmetry
- Limit cycle oscillations â†’ self-sustained terms like (1 - x^2)*v (Van der Pol) or v^3 (Rayleigh) that generate stable periodic orbits
- External periodic driving â†’ additive sinusoidal or cosinusoidal function of time (sin(c*t) or cos(c*t))
- Parametric excitation â†’ position multiplied by a time-dependent oscillatory function (e.g., x*sin(c*t))
- Amplitude-dependent frequency â†’ presence of nonlinear restoring terms (x^3) makes frequency a function of amplitude (backbone curve)
- Conservative oscillator â†’ acceleration depends only on x, no v term (energy conserving)
- Non-conservative oscillator â†’ acceleration includes v terms, indicating energy addition or dissipation
